I guess some people might want to learn some vocabulary for a place they're going, so this one is perhaps also less contrived than some of the other ones. And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated). But I suspect we differ in how interesting we find one vs the other."

          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

But even if the AI was much smarter, it would be a limitation that images are not allowed (for showing e.g. traffic signs).\n\nI also asked about Norwegian words for travel. I guess some people might want to learn some vocabulary for a place they're going, so this one is perhaps also less contrived than some of the other ones. But even if the translations were perfect (I would say there was a fair amount of room for improvement), it is a limitation that there is no sound.\n\n> (ex things like \"maybe card creation should be a multi-turn conversation\" or \"what if we used AI to edit individual cards\")\nIf I wanted to do a \"best effort\" at AI-generated flashcards, then yes I would probably make things multi-turn as you mention (both before and after the first iteration of cards).\n\nAnd probably I would also allow the user to upload/reference material based on which the generate the flashcards. Although for school children with school books, it's a limitation that in general it may not be so easy to provide the relevant pages for the AI to read in a smooth way.\n\nI do think additional ingredients probably would be needed to make this more compelling. And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated). But I suspect we differ in how interesting we find one vs the other."

          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

But even if the AI was much smarter, it would be a limitation that images are not allowed (for showing e.g. traffic signs).\n\nI also asked about Norwegian words for travel. I guess some people might want to learn some vocabulary for a place they're going, so this one is perhaps also less contrived than some of the other ones. But even if the translations were perfect (I would say there was a fair amount of room for improvement), it is a limitation that there is no sound.\n\n> (ex things like \"maybe card creation should be a multi-turn conversation\" or \"what if we used AI to edit individual cards\")\nIf I wanted to do a \"best effort\" at AI-generated flashcards, then yes I would probably make things multi-turn as you mention (both before and after the first iteration of cards).\n\nAnd probably I would also allow the user to upload/reference material based on which the generate the flashcards. Although for school children with school books, it's a limitation that in general it may not be so easy to provide the relevant pages for the AI to read in a smooth way.\n\nI do think additional ingredients probably would be needed to make this more compelling. And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated). But I suspect we differ in how interesting we find one vs the other."

          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated).           "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated).           "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

And as mention I think think one such ingredient could be to enable the rote memorization to be practiced in \"game mode\" (having one or more games where the question-answer pairs are baked in somehow).\n\nI do think there is a lot to be said for curriculums that are \"mass produced\" with most of the work done by AI, but not generated on the fly.\n\nSome of the reasons being:\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve images.\n\u2022 It's easier then to involve audio.\n\u2022 It's perhaps easier then to focus on question-answer pairs that lend themselves to games.\nBut I also understand that the customizability of \"on the fly generation\" is valuable.\n\nAs touched upon earlier, I think we both agree that the \"optimal app\" within this area would use a hybrid model (both generated and pre-generated).           "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."

          "ts": "1784472056.560589",
          "user_id": "U7DJZAQ3G",
          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."
        },
        {

        {
          "ts": "1784472056.560589",
          "user_id": "U7DJZAQ3G",
          "user_name": "Tor",
          "text": "For my Norwegian experiment I removed 4 out of the 10 suggestions. But I guess the line between \"Wrong\" and \"Correct\" is not binary for something like this. There is an in-between area of \"Not that good\".\n\nFor example, it translates \"Please\" with \"Vennligst\". But there is not a 1-to-1 mapping between those words, and \"Vennligst\" is not used that frequently in practice (I think that as I use it now, it may be the first time in my life actually, but who knows).\n\nI think we rely more on \"Could you\" (\"Kunne du\"), or \"Sorry, could you\" (\"Unnskyld, kunne du\"), than \"Please\". And I'm not sure if it's just me, but to me the connotations of \"Vennligst\" feel a bit more passive-aggressive/domineering somehow compared to \"Please\" (but \"Please\" can also have some of that).\n\nFWIW, this feels contrived, since even if all the flashcards were really great there would be no sound. So an app that is serious about wanting to cover language learning would need some system in place for supporting that. Might involve \"pre-processed word pairs\", such that even if something custom is generated for a particular user the pre-processed pairs are made use of."
        },

### 1. Process Slack Captures (`slack`)

4. **Determine Target Folder and Path based on Reaction Type:**

     - Since this is an **Input**, bypass the inbox! Save the file under: `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inputs/Slack/`

       ```yaml

       id: '<timestamp_id>'  # YYYYMMDDHHmmss format based on message ts
       daily_note: "[[Daily Notes/YYYY-MM-DD Weekday|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
       category: "[[Slack]]"
       channel: "<channel_name>"
       original_url: "<permalink>"

         - "<Participant A>"
         - "<Participant B>"
       ---
       ```
     - **Body Layout:**
       Keep standard Slack logs minimalist. No point-by-point summaries, thoughts, or decisions in the body. Only:

       - **Channel:** #<channel_name>

       - **Original Link:** [Slack Thread](<permalink>)

### 4. Process Telegram Captures (`telegram`)
If there are items under the `telegram` key, process them one by one:
1. Determine the date of the conversation (from the `started_at` ISO string) in YYYY-MM-DD format.
2. Determine a spaced capitalized Title based on the topic.
3. Since this is an **Input**, bypass the inbox! Save the file under: `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inputs/Telegram/`
4. Generate the Note Content:
   - **Filename:** `YYYY-MM-DD - Telegram - [Title].md`
   - **Properties (Frontmatter):**
     ```yaml
     ---
     id: '<timestamp_id>'  # YYYYMMDDHHmmss format based on started_at
     daily_note: "[[Daily Notes/YYYY-MM-DD Weekday|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
     category: "[[Telegram]]"
     ---
     ```
   - **Note Body Layout:**
     ```markdown
     # 📥 Telegram Capture: [Title]

     - **Date:** YYYY-MM-DD

     ## Summary
     <A concise, high-quality markdown summary of the Telegram chat session synthesizing the main discussion, key takeaways, and conclusions.>
     ```
     *Crucial rule:* Do NOT include any transcript highlights or transcript sections. Only the `Summary` section is needed.
5. **Integrations:**
   - Run the command to mark the Telegram session as processed:
     `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/fetch_telegram_brains.py --mark-processed <session_id>`
   - Run the light integration pass (appending to `Utilities/log.md` with daily note link).
   - Run `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/integrate_entities.py Inputs/Telegram/<filename> [--gist "..."]` to sync project hub states.

---
### 5. Reporting
At the end, report on all items processed from Slack, Linear, Emails, and Telegram. Keep descriptions concise and formatted for Telegram delivery.
